			</svg>
		</button></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The success of datacenter exits is reflected in customer migrations already executed at scale. For example, <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/26302-copeland-azure" target="_blank">Copeland used Azure Data Box</a> to migrate more than 300 terabytes of data to Azure during a time-sensitive datacenter transition while maintaining business continuity.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/26302-copeland-azure#customers-share-modal-dialog" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Learn how Copeland rebuilt Connect+ on Azure</a></div>
</div>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="ai-and-machine-learning-data-readiness">AI and machine learning data readiness</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For AI and machine learning readiness, organizations need large volumes of high-quality data to be centralized, accessible, and continuously updated. Azure Data Box can support rapid ingestion of massive training datasets, research archives, or historical data. Azure Storage Mover can support ongoing synchronization and pipeline updates, helping data remain current for model training, experimentation, analytics, and AI development.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="backup-media-archives-and-long-term-retention">Backup, media archives, and long-term retention</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For backup, media archives, and long-term retention, organizations often need to move large volumes of infrequently accessed data while maintaining durability, accessibility, and cost efficiency. <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/databox" target="_blank">Azure Data Box</a> can support efficient transfer of large archival datasets, while Azure Storage tiers help optimize cost over time. Azure Storage Mover can support post-migration workflows where ongoing access or updates are required.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This approach is reflected in <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/25537-wnet-azure-virtual-desktop" target="_blank">how The WNET Group modernized its media archive</a>. Using Azure Data Box, WNET migrated approximately 3.6 petabytes of content, representing more than 800,000 hours of media, to <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us" target="_blank">Azure</a>. The move enabled a datacenter exit while maintaining continuous broadcast operations, reduced asset retrieval times from up to 24 hours to under four hours and positioned the organization to apply machine learning for metadata enrichment and content discovery.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/25537-wnet-azure-virtual-desktop" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">See how The WNET Group modernized with Azure Data Box</a></div>
</div>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="healthcare-regulated-and-mission-critical-systems">Healthcare, regulated, and mission-critical systems</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For healthcare, regulated, and mission-critical systems, migration must balance security, compliance, governance, and operational continuity. Azure Migrate can help assess dependencies and support controlled sequencing. Azure Data Box can enable offline transfer for large sensitive datasets. Azure Storage Mover can support incremental updates where ongoing synchronization is required.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/24804-astellas-azure-data-box" target="_blank">Astellas Pharma used Azure Data Box to transfer a 500-terabyte local file share</a> to Azure and meet a six-month migration timeline that enabled the closure of six global datacenters. For regulated industries, this shows how offline transfer can help organizations move quickly while maintaining continuity and control over critical data.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/24804-astellas-azure-data-box#customers-share-modal-dialog" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Learn how Astellas Pharma moved to Azure</a></div>
</div>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="from-migration-execution-to-modernization-outcomes">From migration execution to modernization outcomes</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Migration is not the objective, it is the enabling step.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Once data is established in Azure, organizations can extend into analytics, artificial intelligence, and cloud-native architecture.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">By aligning <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/azure-migrate" target="_blank">Azure Migrate</a>, <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/storage-mover" target="_blank">Azure Storage Mover</a>, and <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/databox" target="_blank">Azure Data Box</a>, organizations gain a migration strategy that reflects real-world conditions while positioning data for long-term value.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="get-started-with-azure-storage-migration-solutions">Get started with Azure Storage migration solutions</h3>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">
  Explore <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/solutions/storage-migration/" target="_blank">Azure Storage and data migration solutions</a> and begin building a migration strategy aligned to your environment, your timelines, and your modernization goals.
</p>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>At Microsoft Build 2026, AI moved from experimentation to execution—shifting from isolated tools to connected systems grounded in business data. Organizations that win will embed AI across workflows, scale it effectively, and translate it into measurable outcomes like faster growth, lower costs, and better customer experiences.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/3-things-leaders-need-to-know-from-microsoft-build-2026/">3 things leaders need to know from Microsoft Build 2026</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">I’ve had a front-row seat to a few major technology advancements—the internet, then cloud, and now agentic AI. Before joining Microsoft, I founded a systems integration business, which means I sat on the other side of the table—the side where you’re trying to figure out which wave is real, what it means for your organization, and whether you’re moving fast enough.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That experience shapes how I think about moments like this one.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Every year, Microsoft Build delivers dozens of news and updates that developers follow closely. Most years, the story is about new capabilities for technical teams to explore. What’s different this year is that these capabilities feel less about exploration and more about meeting expectations to reshape how organizations operate, compete, and deliver results.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">If you’re not a developer, Build can feel pretty technical, and it’s not always immediately obvious how the announcements can translate into business growth or savings. So I want to share a few of my takeaways for business leaders wanting a fast pass understanding of what matters most.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-bloginabox-theme-ump-embed wp-block-msx-ump-embed" class="wp-block-bloginabox-theme-ump-embed">
	<div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">

<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="1-your-ai-is-only-as-good-as-what-it-knows-about-your-business">1. Your AI is only as good as what it knows about your business</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Models matter, but lasting advantage increasingly comes from how well AI understands your business—your unique data, your processes, and how your organization operates.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Every time a team deploys a new AI project, they run into the same problem—the AI starts without that context. It doesn’t know your customers the way your sales team does. It doesn’t understand your definitions of revenue, risk, or success. And as a result, every new project starts from scratch.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That’s why context has become a scaling issue. If every AI project has to rebuild the same foundation, organizations lose time, consistency, and momentum. That’s the gap we focused on closing at Build.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>What this looks like in practice: A shared intelligence foundation for your entire organization</strong>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/microsoft-iq" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft IQ</a> introduces an enterprise intelligence layer where your data, processes, and organizational knowledge have live connections across every AI system, so new agents can start with an understanding of your business and improve as usage grows.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That shared intelligence layer moved from vision to reality with general availability. <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/blog/2026/06/02/announcing-the-new-work-iq-apis/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Work IQ</a> helps AI understand how people work and how the business operates. <a href="https://aka.ms/Azure-Data-Build26" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Fabric IQ</a> connects business data across systems and <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-in/power-platform/products/power-bi" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Power BI</a>. <a href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/build-smarter-agents-faster-with-foundry-iq/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Foundry IQ</a> extends that grounding into deployed applications in Azure, unstructured data, and custom sources. Together, they help agents work from the same business context across the systems your organization relies on.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We also introduced <a href="https://blogs.bing.com/search/June-2026/Announcing-Microsoft-Web-IQ" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Web IQ</a> in limited preview as the newest member of the layer, bringing real-world context from outside the organization.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Together, these layers help agents work from the same business context across the systems your organization relies on. With that shared context in place, the next step is making the models themselves reflect your business.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">And, with <a href="https://microsoft.ai/news/building-a-hillclimbing-machine-launching-seven-new-mai-models/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">capabilities like Frontier Tuning</a>, organizations can fine-tune models using their own data and workflows, reducing costs by up to 10x while improving response speed.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This is especially significant because we’re moving from AI that knows a lot about the world to AI that knows a lot about your world. For business leaders, that’s the difference between a generic tool and a system that reflects how your organization actually operates—maximizing your own data and expertise with AI systems for competitive advantage.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="2-tools-don-t-transform-organizations-systems-do">2. Tools don&#8217;t transform organizations. Systems do.</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Most organizations have accumulated a collection of AI tools. A pilot here, an assistant there, a proof of concept that worked well enough to expand. What they haven’t built yet is an industrialized system designed for end-to-end production at scale.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The distinction matters. Individual tools produce individual results. A system that shares context, enforces governance, and gets smarter the longer it runs.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This was front and center at Build this year, and its core to how we’ve built Azure.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>What this looks like in practice: An integrated platform for building, running, and governing agents at scale</strong>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Built on Azure, the <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Agent Platform</a> brings together what organizations need to build, run, govern, and scale agents across the business. It’s the foundation for moving agents out of pilots and into production—and it’s designed to solve three challenges that consistently slow that transition down.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The first challenge is speed: moving from a promising prototype to something the business can actually run. <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-fabric/features/rayfin">Rayfin</a> helps close that gap by making it easier to go from concept to enterprise-grade deployment, with security, data management, and governance built in from the start.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The second challenge is modernization. Once AI starts touching core business systems, those systems need to evolve continuously, not through large, disruptive transformation cycles. <a href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/AppsonAzureBlog/closing-the-ai-readiness-gap-with-agentic-modernization/4524011" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">New agentic capabilities</a> in Azure help teams update, integrate, and improve applications in parallel and on an ongoing basis, so systems can keep pace with the business without slowing operations down.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">And the third challenge is trust at scale. As more agents move into production, governance and security need to be part of the system from the beginning. That’s why Azure brings together <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/ai-foundry" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Foundry</a>, <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-agent-365" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Agent 365</a>, <a href="https://aka.ms/aca/build" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Azure Container Apps</a>, and the broader Microsoft Security stack to help organizations run agents with controls built in from the moment they start operating.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The winners of this era won’t be the organizations with the most AI tools. They’ll be the ones that build the best system around them.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="3-the-bar-has-moved-ai-is-expected-to-deliver-real-business-outcomes">3. The bar has moved. AI is expected to deliver real business outcomes.</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">It would be easy to read the Build announcements as something to watch from the sidelines. But your board or C-Suite might have other ideas. There’s a version of this moment where business leaders read the Build announcements and think, <em>interesting, I’ll keep watching</em>. Your board or C-suite might already be several steps ahead.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Why? Because the question organizations were asking a year ago, <em>does AI actually work?</em>, has been answered. The question now is different: <em>why isn’t it running significant parts of our business yet?</em></p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In other words, AI is now expected to deliver measurable outcomes—like faster cycle times, lower costs, and improved customer experiences—not just insights or experimentation.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>What this looks like in practice: Enterprise-ready choice, control, and resilience</strong>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Foundry now offers the broadest selection of frontier models in the industry—from OpenAI’s GPT-5 series to the latest from Anthropic and Fireworks AI’s open-weight lineup—all with security and governance built in. We also entered the frontier model space at Build with a new family of enterprise-ready MAI models, giving organizations more control over cost, performance, and how AI is applied to specific business scenarios. The business point is not simply model choice. It’s the ability to shape AI around your own data, workflows, and needs so it can deliver better outcomes at lower cost.</p>



<div class="alignright wp-block-bloginabox-theme-kicker" data-bi-an="Kicker Left">
	<div class="kicker">
		<h2 class="kicker__title">
			Microsoft Discovery helps BHP’s copper innovation		</h2>
		<p class="kicker__content">
							<a
					href="https://news.microsoft.com/signal/articles/microsoft-discovery-bhp-copper/"
					class="kicker__link"
					target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer"				>
						Learn more							↗</a>
					</p>
	</div>
</div>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That control matters most when AI moves beyond assistance and into deep, scientific, and engineering work. <a href="https://aka.ms/MicrosoftDiscoveryBlog" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Discovery</a>, our agentic AI platform for scientific research and complex problem-solving, is now generally available. It uses specialized AI agents to dig through research, generate hypotheses, run simulations, and refine results in continuous loops—compressing timelines that used to take years into months. This is the shift business leaders should pay attention to: AI is beginning to compress the timeline for work that used to take long cycles of research, analysis, and iteration.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">To support that shift, the infrastructure is also changing. <a href="https://aka.ms/GPUAcceleratedFabricDW" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">GPU-accelerated Fabric Data Warehouse</a> delivers up to 7x faster query performance for AI-scale workloads, relative to three comparable external vendors for reporting and application workloads at 64-user. <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/new-azure-cobalt-200-vms-deliver-50-performance-improvement-fully-optimized-for-modern-agentic-ai-workloads/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Azure Cobalt 200 VMs</a> bring purpose-built cloud infrastructure for AI-native workloads.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">And <a href="https://techcommunity.microsoft.com/blog/reliability-and-resiliency-in-azure/announcing-azure-infrastructure-resiliency-manager-public-preview/4523710?" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Infrastructure Resiliency Manager</a> helps organizations plan for resilience when AI is running real operations.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The net is production readiness: giving organizations the control, speed, compute, and resilience they need to run AI in the parts of the business where performance matters.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="your-next-step-to-build-an-ai-powered-business">Your next step to build an AI-powered business</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For me, the throughline is how expectation has replaced experimentation.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">AI is now embedded in workflows, connected across systems, and expected to deliver meaningful outcomes.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For business leaders, the implication is strategic and immediate. The question is no longer whether AI works, but where and how it should be running in your business right now. That means using the next planning cycle to ask a more operational set of questions:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Where are we still treating AI as an isolated pilot instead of connecting it to core workflows?</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Where do we need shared data and context before another tool or model will make a difference?</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Which prototypes are ready to move into production, where value can actually be realized?</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Which AI initiatives are tied directly to business outcomes like cost reduction, speed, and customer impact?</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Where should AI be running meaningful parts of the business today, not next year?</li>
</ul>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Your competitive advantage won’t come from experimenting with AI. It will come from how quickly you put it to work with a solid system that’s grounded in your own intelligence and run on a foundation you can trust.</p>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>Claude Fable 5, Anthropic’s latest Frontier model, available today in Microsoft Foundry, powering agents in GitHub Copilot and Foundry Agent Service.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/claude-fable-5-is-now-available-in-microsoft-foundry-powering-the-next-era-of-autonomous-agents/">Claude Fable 5 available today in Microsoft Foundry: Powering the next era of autonomous agents</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<div class="wp-block-bloginabox-theme-post-alert" role="alert" aria-live="polite" data-bi-an="alert">
	<div class="alert-content">
		Anthropic has disabled Claude Fable 5 and Claude Mythos 5 access globally to comply with a US government export control directive citing national security authorities. All other models remain available. Learn more: <a href="http://www.anthropic.com/news/fable-mythos-access">www.anthropic.com/news/fable-mythos-access</a>	</div>
</div>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Claude Fable 5</a>, Anthropic’s latest frontier model, is available today in <a href="https://ai.azure.com/">Microsoft Foundry</a>, powering agents in <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/github/Copilot" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">GitHub Copilot</a> and <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/ai-foundry/agent-service/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Foundry Agent Service</a>. Claude Fable 5 makes Mythos-level capabilities available to all customers, with strong safeguards designed to make it safe for general use.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link has-text-align-center wp-element-button" href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">See what&#8217;s new in Claude Fable 5</a></div>
</div>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Fable 5</a> is designed for long-running, multi-stage, and asynchronous tasks like complex code refactoring, deep research synthesis, and document-heavy workflows. This elevated level of autonomy changes what teams can ask AI to do. Enterprises can now delegate sophisticated multi-turn projects to agents, enabling them to reason over your organization&#8217;s data to solve real problems.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For enterprises, this frontier capability is only part of the equation. To turn autonomy into real business impact, <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">organizations need a platform to evaluate, ground, govern, deploy, and scale</a> these systems in production.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That is where <a href="https://ai.azure.com/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry</a> comes in. Foundry brings Anthropic’s next generation of intelligence into the broader Microsoft agent platform, helping enterprises build ambitious, high-impact AI solutions on Azure with the security, governance, reliability, and operational controls required for real business workflows.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Combined with <a href="https://aka.ms/MicrosoftIQ" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft IQ</a>, Fable 5 can reason over your team, your knowledge, and your data across Power BI, your applications, and the web, with a continuously updating view that learns as usage grows.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="the-next-generation-of-frontier-intelligence">The next generation of frontier intelligence</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">According to Anthropic, <a href="https://www.anthropic.com/news/claude-fable-5-mythos-5">Claude Fable 5</a> is the next generation of intelligence for the hardest knowledge work and coding problems. It can handle tasks previous models couldn’t sustain and represents a step change in what teams can hand off to Claude.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Claude Fable 5 can plan its approach, check progress against the goal, and refine its work as it goes, instead of waiting for the next instruction. This makes it well suited for complex coding tasks, research workflows, and long-running knowledge work where the model needs to reason across multiple steps.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With improved vision capabilities, <a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Claude Fable 5</a> is also a strong fit for multimodal projects involving documents, PDFs, diagrams, charts, and dense tables. It does not just read the words on a page; it can interpret the meaning carried by visual and structured information. When critical context is embedded in a chart, schematic, or complex table, Claude Fable 5 can take it in and reason over it, helping finance, legal, analytics, and architecture teams work through material that is often reviewed manually today.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="claude-fable-5-real-world-enterprise-use-cases">Claude Fable 5 real-world enterprise use cases</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For business leaders, <a href="https://www.anthropic.com/news/claude-fable-5-mythos-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Claude Fable 5</a> changes how knowledge work is accomplished across the organization. Fable 5 is a frontier general-purpose model designed to help support complex, cross-functional tasks that span reasoning, creation, and execution.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><strong>Key enterprise use cases include:</strong></p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Software development:</strong> Supporting demanding coding and system-level builds that stretch across days and stages, by carrying context from analysis through implementation and review.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Financial services:</strong> Building investment research, working through earnings, weighing credit and risk, and supporting compliance workflows—including the numbers locked inside long filings and their exhibits.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><strong>Legal:</strong> Marking up and reviewing contracts, streamlining due diligence, digging through case law, and producing first-pass motions and memos.</li>
</ul>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Beyond these, Claude Fable 5 also carries professional work across marketing, sales, and analytics, shaping strategy, drawing out insight, and turning it into decision-ready output as part of connected, end-to-end workflows.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="built-with-safeguards-for-responsible-use">Built with safeguards for responsible use</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">According to Anthropic, <a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Claude Fable 5</a> is being introduced with additional safeguards that reflect the company’s approach to responsible AI development. Because the model has advanced capabilities in sensitive domains such as cybersecurity, biology, and chemistry, Anthropic has placed limits on how far the broadly available version will go in those areas. Beyond the model’s built-in safeguards, Microsoft Foundry provides developers with advanced guardrails and controls, as well as robust observability and security capabilities in Foundry Control Plane. Last week at Build, we announced <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/guardrails/guided-set-up" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">guided guardrail setup</a>, which walks developers through a few questions about an agent’s users, data, tools, and actions, then recommends and applies the right controls at the right intervention points, tailored to each agent’s scenario. These enterprise grade responsible AI features help developers govern, monitor, and manage AI systems and agent fleets.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For a small set of select users, including participants in <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/msrc/blog/2026/04/strengthening-secure-software-global-scale-how-msrc-is-evolving-with-ai" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Project Glasswing</a>, Anthropic is also offering Claude Mythos 5. Mythos 5 is a version of the same model intended for internal, defensive use with those domain restrictions removed. This approach allows Anthropic to make most of Claude Fable 5’s frontier capabilities broadly available while continuing to refine safeguards for higher-risk use cases.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For enterprise customers, this means access to advanced autonomous capabilities with a clearer safety posture, which is an important consideration when deploying AI systems in real business environments.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="why-microsoft-foundry">Why Microsoft Foundry?</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Access to a powerful model like Claude Fable 5 is only the starting point. The real challenge for enterprises is <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/the-economics-of-enterprise-ai-what-the-forrester-tei-study-reveals-about-microsoft-foundry/">operationalizing autonomous AI securely, reliably, and in alignment with organizational policies</a>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As Jay Parikh, Executive Vice President of CoreAI at Microsoft, <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">recently said</a>:</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow has-quote-default-font-size">

<p class="has-large-font-size wp-block-paragraph">The winners won’t be those with the most demos, but those that turn AI into a governed, continuously improving system for running real work.</p>

</blockquote>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That is why platform matters. Microsoft’s agent platform spanning GitHub, Microsoft IQ, Foundry, Agent 365, Azure, and Microsoft 365, gives organizations the foundation to build, ground, govern, and improve AI systems at scale.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://aka.ms/MicrosoftIQ" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft IQ</a> plays a critical role by connecting agents to enterprise context across Microsoft 365, business systems, and knowledge bases, so models like Claude Fable 5 can reason with the right organizational context instead of operating in isolation.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">With <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry</a>, customers can turn frontier models into enterprise-ready solutions. They can evaluate and deploy Claude Fable 5 alongside other Claude models, apply platform-level security and governance controls, integrate AI into existing workflows, and scale from pilot to production with identity, access management, and operational controls built in.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="pricing">Pricing</h2>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-fixed-layout"><tbody><tr><td><strong>Model</strong></td><td><strong>Input/1M Tokens</strong></td><td><strong>Output/1M Tokens</strong></td></tr><tr><td>Claude Fable 5</td><td>$10</td><td>$50</td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="moving-from-experimentation-to-impact">Moving from experimentation to impact</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models/claude-fable-5" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Claude Fable 5</a>’s arrival on <a href="https://ai.azure.com/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Foundry</a> marks a milestone for enterprises ready to tackle more ambitious problems, streamline complex workflows, and enhance productivity across the organization. By bringing Claude Fable 5 to Foundry, Azure enables organizations to move faster, from experimentation to real, accelerated business impact without compromising on trust or control.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Ready to explore what autonomous AI can do for your organization? Access Claude Fable 5 today in <a href="https://ai.azure.com/catalog/models">Foundry Models</a>, <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/ai-foundry/agent-service/">Foundry Agent Service</a>, and <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/github/Copilot">GitHub Copilot</a>.</p>

		<item>
		<title>AI alone won’t change your business. The system running it will.</title>
		<link>https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/</link>
					<comments>https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Jay Parikh]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Tue, 02 Jun 2026 19:15:57 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[AI + machine learning]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[AI]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/?p=51577</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>We are building a comprehensive agent platform: one that supports many models, is open, and gives you flexibility at every layer of the stack.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/">AI alone won’t change your business. The system running it will.</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">AI has arrived in the enterprise, and the shift is happening all at once. Every function, every role, every workflow is being reshaped. At the same time, a new class of organizations is emerging, one that will look fundamentally different from the companies that defined the last era of business. The winners won’t be those with the most demos, but those that turn AI into a governed, continuously improving system for running real work.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This isn’t just about chatbots, either. Those experiences are useful, but they don’t transform how large organizations operate. The real opportunity is teams of agents executing long running work across functions like software delivery, support, finance, HR, and operations — with the identity, context, policy, and human oversight required to trust them in production.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">To make this possible, enterprises need more than access to a powerful AI model or scalable compute. What determines success is the system around the AI: how agents are built and deployed by engineering teams, how they’re contextualized in the enterprise, how they’re governed and observed in production, and how they improve safely over time. Without that system, AI remains fragmented, fragile, and difficult to trust at scale.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We’re taking a fundamentally different approach. We are building a comprehensive agent platform: one that supports many models, is open, and gives you choice and flexibility at every layer of the stack. And we are purposefully designing it with developers at the center. Today, the next pieces of that platform are clicking into place.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Building a system for the agentic enterprise<br>To succeed in this new era, an agent platform must meet a higher bar. It must run real production workloads, map real organizational complexity, and manage real business responsibility.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We’re building around three key principles:</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">First, it must be a single, integrated system, with support for a wide range of models.<br>Enterprises can’t afford to assemble their agent strategy one piece at a time. Disconnected tools stitched together after the fact can slow teams down and introduce unnecessary risk. Building, contextualizing, running, governing, and improving agents should happen within one coherent system. That’s why we’re bringing together Azure, GitHub, Microsoft IQ, Fabric, Foundry, Windows, Microsoft Security, and Microsoft 365 to operate as a single system you can use to deploy agents at enterprise scale. Enterprises also need the flexibility to choose the right model for the task, balancing quality, speed, and cost — including Microsoft models, partner models, and open models.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Second, it must be secured and governed by design.<br>Governance is easy to claim and much harder to deliver. Making it real means starting with a single stack that spans development through production, built on the identity, access, compliance, and security foundations enterprises already trust. By extending Entra, Purview, Defender, Agent 365, and the broader Microsoft Security stack, governance becomes native to the system rather than bolted on later, supporting the ambitions of an AI first enterprise without compromising control.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Third, it must improve continuously.<br>Enterprise AI systems can’t be static. Agent behavior, outcomes, and human feedback must flow back into the system, so it can improve safely over time under human oversight. As the system runs, models, workflows, and agents become more capable and more specific to an enterprise’s unique business processes. The result is a system that compounds in value the longer it’s in use.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">These properties are becoming must-haves, and enterprises that align their AI ambitions with these three principles will pull ahead in quarters, not years.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">So how does a system like this actually take shape inside a real enterprise? It starts where work begins, with how agents are built. Let’s walk through what that looks like on the platform we’ve built.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A diagram of the Microsoft agent platform, with a box at the top with the line: One enterprise system. Six boxes below the top box, all in one line, labeled from left to right: 01 Build GitHub; 02 Contextualize Microsoft IQ; 03 Run Microsoft Foundry; 04 Govern Agent 365; 05 Improve Foundry optimization; 06 Surface Teams | Microsoft 365.</p>



<ol class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Build in GitHub</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">GitHub is where your developers already work. It’s where your dependencies live, where your application and code context is kept, where you collaborate with the open source community you depend on, and where you drive innovation. Building agents anywhere else means leaving all that behind.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agents should be built the same way production software is built. You write code with GitHub Copilot to move faster. You bring together the assets that matter most: codebases, work items, agent skills, and tools. And because agents aren’t just code, you bring your evals and observability assets alongside them, all versioned the way any production system should be.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agents must follow a lifecycle: source, test, deploy, observe, and improve. GitHub sets up that lifecycle and provides the necessary controls from day one. The result is a workflow designed for building agents with the right guardrails from the start. And you can do all this in one place, in a new app built for this system.</p>



<ol start="2" class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Contextualize with Microsoft IQ</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Code is only part of an agent. To be useful, an agent also has to understand your business: your customers, your products, your contracts, your processes. Without enterprise context and intelligence you can trust, even the most capable model is guessing.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Enterprises require a wide variety of models and the ability to match the right model to the right job, but model choice alone is not enough. Microsoft IQ grounds agents in enterprise context by connecting to your business data wherever it lives, across Microsoft 365, your core business systems (such as customer and revenue data), and other systems your enterprise already relies on, like knowledge bases and your website. With Web IQ, the latest addition to the IQ platform, agents can also incorporate relevant information from the web when appropriate.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Contextualizing agents in enterprise data isn’t just about access. Pointing AI at raw information is inefficient and brittle. Microsoft IQ organizes, secures, and surfaces the right information in forms agents can actually use, so they can reach accurate insight without drowning in noise or hallucinating answers.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Once agents are grounded in the right context, enterprises can go further. With Frontier Tuning, you don’t just call AI models. You improve how they behave using your data and real-world workflows.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">That includes Microsoft’s seven new MAI models, spanning image, voice, transcription, coding, and reasoning. Together, this model family is designed to work across the kinds of tasks that matter in the real world, and critically, these models are not static endpoints. They’re built to learn from how work actually gets done in your business.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Our reinforcement learning environments allow our models to be reinforced through actual outcomes in your environment. Think of them as training gyms for AI. Here the agent learns your very specific processes, standards, and way of working. It becomes specialized and adapted to you, delivering a measurable and better ROI.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Moreover, your custom or post-trained models all stay in your environment. Your intellectual property, your proprietary data, and the way work actually gets done become part of how your agents reason and act. The resulting intelligence runs in your environment, under your control, and the learning stays yours.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Without context and Frontier Tuning, agents are capable generalists. With it, they become a customized partner that understands the business they’re operating in.</p>



<ol start="3" class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Run in Foundry</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Once agents are built and contextualized, they need a place to run. Not as an experiment. In production.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agents and teams of agents place very different demands on a runtime than traditional applications do. They need to reason, act, call tools, coordinate with other agents, and adapt over time, all while operating under enterprise controls. Foundry is the runtime designed for that reality.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The largest collection of models: Different agents need to be good at different things at different price points. Whatever the task, whatever the cost profile, Foundry provides access to the right model, and an optimized model router helps you balance quality, speed, and cost for each agent.<br>Optimized performance for open models: With Fireworks AI on Foundry, enterprises get faster, more efficient inference directly into the platform.<br>Support for any agent, including those not built on our stack: Bring in agents built on the Microsoft Agent Framework, LangGraph, GitHub Copilot SDK, Claude Agent SDK, or a custom harness.<br>Tools and actions: Agents act on enterprise systems through MCP, connectors, APIs, and workflows, with safe execution by default.<br>Evals and traces: Observability and traces make agent behavior measurable. If you can’t measure it, you can’t improve it.<br>Continuous optimization: Foundry enables tuning of models, harnesses, IQs, tools, and actions over time, improving performance as agents operate in your world.<br>A trust, security, and policy rail wraps the entire runtime. Policy applies consistently across context access, tool calls, optimization updates, traces, and response delivery. The agent doesn’t just work. It works the way your enterprise requires.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This is where your agent stops being a project and starts becoming a production system.</p>



<ol start="4" class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Govern with Agent 365</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Now multiply that agent by hundreds. Then thousands. That’s what happens as different teams build agents across an enterprise. Some are well designed. Some aren’t. Some have access they shouldn’t. Others are doing valuable work that no one else in the organization benefits from.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Enterprise governance isn’t optional. Enterprises need a way to see what’s running, understand what it can access, monitor task adherence, and enforce policies across their entire agent estate.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agent 365, along with Entra, Purview, Defender, and the broader Microsoft Security stack, come together to do just this. And if you’re interested in AI for security in addition to securing your AI, there’s “MDASH.”</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Every agent in your organization shows up in a single catalog, whether it was built in Foundry or elsewhere. IT sees who deployed an agent, what data and tools it can access, how it’s behaving, and what it costs. They can enforce policy or take action when required.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">One place. Full visibility. Real control over what your agents do and don’t do.</p>



<ol start="5" class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Improve continuously</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agents can’t be static. Every agent action generates signal: trajectories, outcomes, feedback. The system captures it, refines it, and feeds it back. Observe. Evaluate. Improve. Roll out safely. Repeat.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This learning loop runs continuously, in production.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Most gains start with eval-driven improvements to the agent itself: prompts, context, skills, and tools. As clear patterns emerge, learning can extend into model routing across multiple models, fine-tuning, or reinforcement learning. But it all stays anchored in evaluation, improving agent quality and ROI to the level the business requires.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The loop is governed, not closed. Enterprises need to audit it, correct it, and control how to roll out changes. The system becomes more capable over time, guided by human oversight and increasingly autonomous, but never beyond your reach.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This is the hill-climbing model in action: system-level improvement, happening continuously while the system runs.</p>



<ol start="6" class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Surface where people work, and scale on Azure</li>
</ol>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Of course, none of this matters if it doesn’t reach the people doing the work.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agents surface directly in the flow of work, in Teams, across Microsoft 365, and inside your own applications and experiences. Identity, security, and compliance are built in from the start, so the agents that your teams rely on day to day inherit the same trust model as the rest of your environment.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We support multiple platforms, but your agents can be developed and run in an optimized and secure way on Windows. You can run models both in the cloud and locally on your machine, and best-in-class sandboxing lets you run always-on agents safely.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">When you need compute optimized for AI, global and sovereign infrastructure, or a route to market, the system scales on Azure, the same enterprise foundation customers have trusted for decades.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The system compounds<br>Every leading enterprise will converge on this model: a central AI platform that orchestrates work across the business, bringing together data, models, agents, and human judgment into a continuously improving and secure system.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As that system runs, its value compounds. Velocity increases and the bottleneck shifts from effort to human creativity and coordination. People are able to do more work independently, guided by shared context and fewer handoffs, while the business moves faster without adding friction.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We’re in a time of profound disruption. The enterprises that lead in this moment will be those that adapt as conditions change, simplify how work is coordinated across the business, and consistently turn intelligence into real outcomes. Microsoft’s agent platform is designed to do exactly that: it unlocks the ability to build, contextualize, run, govern, and improve agents as a single, integrated system.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">At that point, the platform becomes more than a build layer. It becomes the operating system for enterprise AI at scale, where intelligence and trust are built in by design.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/">AI alone won’t change your business. The system running it will.</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>

	<div id="accordion-collapse-56113823-fe94-4150-a7bb-4e44cb20d51c" class="table-of-contents-block__collapse-wrapper collapse show" data-parent="#accordion-56113823-fe94-4150-a7bb-4e44cb20d51c">
		<div class="table-of-contents-block__content">
			<ol class="table-of-contents-block__list"><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#how-microsoft-discovery-supports-r-d-workflows-at-scale">How Microsoft Discovery supports R&amp;D workflows at scale</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#expanding-access-with-the-microsoft-discovery-app-preview">Expanding access with the Microsoft Discovery app preview</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#applying-microsoft-discovery-across-r-d">Applying Microsoft Discovery across R&amp;D</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#get-started-today-with-microsoft-discovery">Get started today with Microsoft Discovery</a></li></ol>		</div>
	</div>
	<span class="table-of-contents-block__progress-bar"></span>
</aside>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Breakthroughs in science and engineering rarely come from a single insight. They emerge through cycles of hypothesis, experimentation, refinement, and review across teams, tools, and data.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Today at Microsoft Build, we are announcing that <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/solutions/discovery/">Microsoft Discovery is now generally available</a> for all organizations, providing a comprehensive platform for building and governing agentic AI workflows across scientific and engineering disciplines. We are also introducing the Microsoft Discovery app in preview, a local desktop experience that helps researchers, students, and scientific teams begin working with Microsoft Discovery today.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/solutions/discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Explore Microsoft Discovery features</a></div>
</div>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Since introducing Microsoft Discovery in private preview <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/transforming-rd-with-agentic-ai-introducing-microsoft-discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">at Microsoft Build last year</a>, we have worked closely with organizations applying AI to complex research and development (R&amp;D) workflows. Their feedback helped reinforce where agentic AI needs to go beyond individual assistance, like supporting the iterative loops, evidence preservation, and tool coordination that define scientific work.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The most challenging problems in R&amp;D require more than just a prompt interface or a single model response. Scientific workflows require:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Integration with institutional knowledge and domain expertise.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Access to specialized modeling, simulation, and analysis tools.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Connection to experimental evidence and validation data.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Support for review processes that shape research decisions.</li>
</ul>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A materials scientist may need to evaluate performance, safety, and cost alongside manufacturability and regulatory constraints. A semiconductor team may need to explore a larger design space without losing physical fidelity or traceability. A life sciences researcher may need to connect literature and experimental data with models and cohort-level evidence before deciding what to validate next.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/microsoft-discovery/overview-what-is-microsoft-discovery" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Discovery is designed to work within these existing R&amp;D environments</a>, not replace them. The platform helps experts understand the reasoning path behind outputs and keeps human judgment at the center of scientific and engineering decisions. The general availability of Microsoft Discovery marks a significant milestone in turning these requirements into a production-ready platform for R&amp;D environments with governance and transparency built in.</p>


<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a3f012cb1d0e&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a3f012cb1d0e" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-large has-custom-border wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-1024x576.webp" alt="Microsoft Discovery initial screen showing the initial welcome landing page asking the individual, &ldquo;What would you like to discover today?&rdquo; with an open prompt box." class="wp-image-51250 webp-format" style="border-top-left-radius:1px;border-top-right-radius:1px;border-bottom-left-radius:1px;border-bottom-right-radius:1px" srcset="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-1024x576.webp 1024w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-300x169.webp 300w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-768x432.webp 768w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-1536x864.webp 1536w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-2048x1152.webp 2048w" data-orig-src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Workspace2-1024x576.webp"><button

<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="how-microsoft-discovery-supports-r-d-workflows-at-scale">How Microsoft Discovery supports R&amp;D workflows at scale</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/solutions/discovery/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft Discovery enables organizations to define agentic workflows</a> around their own R&amp;D programs. Teams can create and coordinate specialized agents, connect those agents to institutional knowledge and external scientific information, and orchestrate work across modeling, simulation, analysis, and validation tools.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">At the center of the platform is <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/microsoft-discovery/concept-discovery-engine">the Microsoft Discovery Engine</a>, which supports the core loop of scientific work by helping teams move from evidence to hypotheses, through execution and analysis, and into the next iteration. This loop allows teams to move beyond isolated analysis toward repeatable, evidence-driven exploration, where they can compare tradeoffs, question assumptions, and narrow a search space in a way that can be reviewed and repeated.</p>


<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a3f012cb307c&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a3f012cb307c" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-large has-custom-border wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-1024x576.webp" alt="Microsoft Discovery Engine interface showing task creation and status overview with completion tracking." class="wp-image-51251 webp-format" style="border-top-left-radius:1px;border-top-right-radius:1px;border-bottom-left-radius:1px;border-bottom-right-radius:1px" srcset="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-1024x576.webp 1024w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-300x169.webp 300w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-768x432.webp 768w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-1536x864.webp 1536w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-2048x1152.webp 2048w" data-orig-src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task1-1024x576.webp"><button

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As we continued product development, we focused on what it takes to <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/microsoft-discovery-advancing-agentic-rd-at-scale/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">bring agentic AI into production R&amp;D environments</a>:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Workflows need to remain reproducible.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Outputs must be reviewable.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Proprietary knowledge must be connected and governed appropriately.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Agentic systems need to fit into the operating model of R&amp;D organizations.</li>
</ul>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Those considerations, along with continued customer feedback, helped shape the general availability release and the platform capabilities behind it.</p>


<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a3f012cb44b5&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a3f012cb44b5" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-large has-custom-border wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-1024x576.webp" alt="Discovery Engine interface displaying a confidence summary table with categorical scores and detailed findings section with inline citations and source references." class="wp-image-51252 webp-format" style="border-top-left-radius:1px;border-top-right-radius:1px;border-bottom-left-radius:1px;border-bottom-right-radius:1px" srcset="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-1024x576.webp 1024w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-300x169.webp 300w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-768x432.webp 768w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-1536x864.webp 1536w, https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-2048x1152.webp 2048w" data-orig-src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/05/Discovery-Task2-1024x576.webp"><button

<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="expanding-access-with-the-microsoft-discovery-app-preview">Expanding access with the Microsoft Discovery app preview</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">An important goal for Microsoft is to make advanced AI and computing capabilities more accessible to the people working on some of today’s most difficult scientific and engineering challenges. Alongside the general availability of Microsoft Discovery, we are introducing the Microsoft Discovery app available in preview today.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The Microsoft Discovery app is a localized experience that gives researchers, students, academic labs, and scientific teams a simpler way to begin using Microsoft Discovery capabilities without starting with a full enterprise deployment. It is available for download on the <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/discovery">Microsoft Discovery GitHub</a> and users can get started with a <a href="https://github.com/features/copilot">GitHub Copilot account</a>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This preview extends Microsoft Discovery to earlier stages of exploration, where research ideas begin as small-team projects, academic work, or individual investigation. <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/discovery">The Microsoft Discovery app</a> is designed to lower the barrier to hands-on exploration, with a practical entry point for literature exploration, hypothesis generation, scientific reasoning, and iterative experimentation.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The app lets researchers explore Microsoft Discovery capabilities using their own working environment. As projects mature and complexity increases, researchers and teams can bring work developed locally into Microsoft Discovery platform to support more advanced R&amp;D programs.</p>



<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a3f012cb5633&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a3f012cb5633" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-full has-custom-border wp-lightbox-container"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1920" height="1020" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/DiscoveryApp_Setup_newlogo.gif" alt="Figure 4: The Microsoft Discovery app welcome screen." class="wp-image-51332" style="border-top-left-radius:1px;border-top-right-radius:1px;border-bottom-left-radius:1px;border-bottom-right-radius:1px" /><button
